Jamison Brereton

32 (548)
Indra
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi (1тАУ25), ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha (26ab), Vasiс╣гс╣нha or ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гtha (26cdтАУ27)
27 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, except dvipad─Б vir─Бj 3, arranged in prag─Бthas
This final hymn in the VIIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala Indra cycle is a loose collection of prag─Бthas, the first of which has a two-p─Бda extension (vs. 3). Even within the verse pairs there is little cohesion. But there is a unifying theme that runs throughout: IndraтАЩs gener ous giving and our grateful receiving, to an extent unusual even in an Indra hymn. Moreover, it is not only IndraтАЩs giving that we seek: it is repeatedly emphasized that Indra helps and gives to mortals who themselves give, that is, the patrons of the sacrifice (see, e.g., vss. 7, 8, 10, 15).
The hymn opens (vs. 1) with the preoccupation that has been visible in many Indra hymns in VII, the fear that rival sacrificers may attract Indra to their own rituals, and IndraтАЩs epithet тАЬinvoked by manyтАЭ appears several times (vss. 17, 20, 26). Much of the hymn is concerned with defining the type of ritual behavior that will cause Indra to choose one sacrifice over another.
Indra is supreme in this hymn. In its twenty-seven verses there is only one men tion of another divinity, the Maruts in verse 10.

Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬLet not, Indra, (other) worshippers detain you far from us; come from whatever distance to ourassembly; present at this ceremony, hear our (prayers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let not (any other) cantors at all stop you at a distance from us.
Even from afar come here to our joint revelry, or being (already) here hearken (to us),

Griffith

LET none, no, not thy worshippers, delay thee far away from us.
Even from far away come thou unto our feast, or listen if already here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the libation is effused for you, these offerers of sacrifice swarm like flies around honey; the piouspraisers, desiring riches, fix their hope upon Indra, like a foot upon a chariot.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because these who craft sacred formulations for you sit like flies on honey when (the soma) is pressed. The singers, seeking goods, set their desire on Indra, like a foot on a chariot.

Jamison Brereton Notes

should be interpreted.

Griffith

For here, like flies on honey, these who pray to thee sit by the juice that they have poured.
Wealth-craving singers have on Indra set their hope, as men set foot upon a car.

Geldner

Denn diese bereiten dir eine Erbauung und sitzen bei dem Soma wie Fliegen auf dem Honig. Auf Indra haben die sch├дtzebegierigen S├дnger ihren Wunsch gesetzt wie den Fu├Я auf den Wagen.

Grassmann

Denn diese Beter sitzen hier bei deinem Trank, wie Fliegen bei dem Honigseim, Auf Indra setzten k├╝hn die S├дnger ihr Begehr, wie auf den Wagen ihren Fuss.

English translation:

тАЬDesirous of riches, I call upon the benevolent wielder of the thunderbolt, as a son upon a father.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Desirous of wealth I call upon the one with mace in hand, possessing a good right (hand/horse) [/bringing good priestly gifts], like a son
upon his father.

Jamison Brereton Notes

sud├бkс╣гiс╣Зa- is a triple pun. In its only other RVic occurrence (VIII.33.5) it means тАШhaving a good right (horse)тАЩ, but it could equally mean тАШhaving a good right (hand)тАЩ, alluding to the immediately preceding v├бjrahasta- тАШhaving the mace in his handтАЩ. And, in keeping with the theme of giving, it can refer to the d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Б-, the priestly giftтАЩ distributed at the dawn sacrifice. This would respond to the r─Бy├бsk─Бma- тАШdesirous of wealthтАЩ, which opens the verse.

Griffith

Longing for wealth I call on him, the Thunderer with the strong right hand,
As a son calleth on his sire.

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra, whose ear is ready to hear, listen to the suppliant for riches, and never disappoint ourprayers; he who is the giver of hundreds and thousands; may no one ever hinder him when willing to give.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He will listen: he of listening ears is implored for goods. He will never neglect our songs.
The one who just in a single day will give hundreds, thousandsтАФno one will confound him when he is about to give.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner joins c with b, rather than d as I do. This is possible, but the topic of giving in both c and d connects them thematically.

Griffith

May he whose ear is open hear us. He is asked for wealth: will he despise our prayer?
Him who bestows at once a hundred thousand gifts none shall restrain when he would give.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe a defence, Maghavan, to the wealthy (offerers in oblations), for you are the discomfiter of (our)adversaries; may we divide the spoil of the enemy slain by you, who are indestructible, bring it to our dwelling.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Be a defense for the bounteous (patrons), bounteous one, when you will herd together those who vaunt themselves.
Might we have a share in the possessions of the one slain by you. Bring here the patrimony of the one difficult to get at.

Griffith

When thou dost drive the fighting men together be, thou Mighty One, the mighty’s shield.
May we divide the wealth of him whom thou hast slain: bring us, Unreachable, his goods.

Geldner

Sei du der Hort unserer G├╢nner, du G├╢nner, wenn du die ├Ьberheblichen zu Paaren treiben wirst. Wir m├╢chten das Besitztum des von dir Erschlagenen unter uns teilen. Bringet uns den Hausrat des Unnahbaren!

Grassmann

Sei, m├дcht’ger, du ein starker Schirm der M├дchtigen, dass du den Feind zu Paaren treibst Und des von dir erschlagnen Schatz uns zuertheilst; des B├╢sen Hausrath f├╝hr uns zu.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPour out the libation to Indra, the thunderer, the drinker of the Soma; prepare the baked (cakes) tosatisfy him; do (what is agreeable to him), for he bestows happiness on (the worshipper) who plural ases them.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Press soma for soma-drinking Indra who holds the mace.
Cook cooked dishes. Just cause (him) to help. It is only the generous giver who is a joy to the one who generously gives.

Jamison Brereton Notes

├бvase kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam is close to a periphrastic causative, since тАЬmake [=create] (him) for helpтАЭ is unlikely to take the long-created Indra as object. Zehnder (p. 7 and passim) takes it as such.

Griffith

For Indra, Soma-drinker, armed with thunder, press the Soma juice.
Make ready your dressed meats: cause him to favour us. The Giver blesses him who gives.

Geldner

Presset dem Somatrinker den Soma, dem Indra, der die Keule hat! Kochet Kochspeisen; machet zur Gnade geneigt! Nur der Freigebige ist dem Freigebigen eine Freude.

Grassmann

Dem Somatrinker Indra presst den Soma, ihm, der Blitze tr├дgt; Die Br├╝hen br├╝ht, zur H├╝lfe schafft ihn auch herbei, der Labsal schenkt dem schenkenden.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOfferers of the libation, do not hesitate; be active; sacrifice to the mighty benefactor for the sake ofriches; the assiduous worshipper conquers (his enemies), dwells in a habitation, and prospers; the gods favournot the imperfect rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na dev─Бsaс╕е karatnave: karatnuс╕е = kutsita kriya, bad or defective act of religion; men donot become gods by such means, dev─Б na bhavanti

Jamison Brereton

You pressers of soma, do not fail; be skillful for the great one. Make (him inclined) to thrust wealth (to us).
It is just the surpassing man who wins: he dwells peacefully, he thrives. The gods are not for the petty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

kс╣Ыс╣Зudhv├бm тАж ─Бt├║je similarly functions as a periphrastic causative. So also Zehnder (p. 20 and passim).

Griffith

Grudge not, ye Soma pourers; stir you, pay the rites, for wealth, to the great Conqueror.
Only the active conquers dwells in peace, and thrives: not for the niggard are the Gods.

Geldner

Bleibt nicht Stecken, ihr Somavollen, machet es dem Gro├Яen recht! Machet, da├Я er Reichtum herausschlage. Nur der Meister gewinnt das Spiel; er wohnt gl├╝cklich, gedeiht. Die G├╢tter sind nicht f├╝r den St├╝mper.

Grassmann

Nicht opfert fehl, o Priester, macht’s dem grossen recht, zur Reichthumsgabe regt ihn an; Wer eifrig ist, der siegt, hat Frieden und gedeiht; dem Kargen sind die G├╢tter feind.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬNo one overturns, no one arrests the chariot of the liberal sacrificer; he, of whom Indra is the protector,of whom the Maruts (are the defenders), will walk in pastures filled with cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

No one has encircled the chariot of Sud─Бs [/the good giver], nor stopped it.
Whoever has Indra as helper, whoever has the Maruts, he will come to a pen full of cattle.

Griffith

No one hath overturned or stayed the car of him who freely gives.
The man whom Indra and the Marut host defend comes to a stable full of kine.

Geldner

Keiner hemmt den Wagen des Freigebigen, noch h├дlt er ihn auf. Wes Helfer Indra und die Marut sind, der gelangt zu rinderreicher H├╝rde.

Grassmann

Den Wagen dess, der reichlich gibt, h├дlt niemand auf, noch hindert ihn; Wem Indra hilft und wem die muntre Marutschar, der kommt zu rinderreichem Stall.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the man of whom you, Indra, are the protector, invigorating (you with praise), enjoy (abundant) food;be the preserver, hero, of our chariots, (the preserver) of our people.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Be the preserver: bodhi avit─Б: bodhi,second person n singular imperative of bu (for bhava), b being substituted for bh

Jamison Brereton

He will come to the prize when he strives for the prizeтАФthe mortal whose helper you will be, Indra.
Become a helper to our chariots, o champion, to our men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although тАШseeking the prizeтАЩ is ordinarily accented as a denominative (v─Бjay├бnt-), as opposed to тАШinciteтАЩ (v─Бj├бya-) with causative accent, in this context, the denominative sense seems clear. See comm. on 14d below.

Griffith

Indra, that man when fighting shall obtain the spoil, whose strong defender thou wilt be.
Be thou the gracious helper, Hero I of our cars, be thou the helper of our men.

Geldner

Zum Siegergewinn gelangt der danach strebende Sterbliche, o Indra, dessen Helfer du wirst. Sei der Helfer unserer Wagen, unserer Mannen, du Held!

Grassmann

Zur Labung kommt der Mann, der dich, o Indra, labt, und dessen F├╢rderer du bist; Sei du, o Held, ein F├╢rdrer unsrer Wagenschar und unsrer M├дnner F├╢rderer.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬVerily (Indra’s) share (of the Soma) exceeds (that of other deities) like the wealth of the victorious;enemies overcome not him, who is the lord of bay steeds, who gives strength to the offerer of the libation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

His share now is outstanding like the spoils of a victor.
Indra of the fallow baysтАФcheats do not outwit him. He places skill in the one who has soma.

Griffith

His portion is exceeding great like a victorious soldier’s spoil.
Him who is Indra, Lord of Bays, no foes subdue. He gives the Soma-pourer strength.

Geldner

Sein Anteil ist der gr├╢├Яte wie der Gewinn des Siegers. Ihn, der der Falbenfahrer Indra ist, hintergehen die Schelme nicht. Den Somavollen verleiht er T├╝chtigkeit.

Grassmann

Der Antheil dessen raget hoch, gleichwie des Siegers Preis hervor, Wem Indra hold ist, den besch├дd’gen Feinde nicht, dem Somabringer gibt er Kraft.

English translation:

тАЬAddress (to Indra), among the gods, the ample, well-uttered, and graceful prayer; many bonds entanglenot him who, by his devotion, abides in Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

A mantraтАФnot stunted, well arranged, well adornedтАФset it among those worthy of the sacrifice.
The many onslaughts never overcome him who through ritual work comes to be in (the good grace) of Indra.

Griffith

Make for the Holy Gods a hymn that is not mean, but well-arranged and fair of form.
Even many snares and bonds subdue not him who dwells with Indra through his sacrifice.

Geldner

Machet ein nicht zu kurzes, wohlgesetztes, zierliches Dichterwort auf die opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter. Auch viele Angriffe bemeistern den nicht, der sich durch Opferdienst bei Indra in Gunst setzt.

Grassmann

Den sch├╢ngemessnen, herrlichen, vollkommnen Spruch, den bringt den hehren G├╢ttern dar; Auch viel Gefahren gehn vor├╝ber an dem Mann, der frommen Werks bei Indra bleibt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhat mortal, Indra, injures him who has you for his support? He who offers you (sacrificial) food,Maghavan, with faith, he obtains food on the day of the libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P─Бrye divi v─Бj─л v─Бjam siс╣г─Бsati = sautyeahani sa haviс╣гm─Бn annam sevate

Jamison Brereton

What mortal will dare against him who has you as his
possession, Indra?
It is with trust in you, bounteous one, that on the decisive day the one vying for the prize seeks to win the prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ыraddh─Б╠Бis most likely instrumental, but its lack of contraction with the following vowel in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text gives pause. See Oldenberg on this problem. 36 v─Бj─л╠Бv─Б╠Бjaс╣Г siс╣г─Бsati seems like a variant of g├бmad v─Б╠Бjam v─Бj├бyan in 11a with different emphasis. See also 20a below.

Griffith

Indra, what mortal will attack the man who hath his wealth in thee?
The strong will win the spoil on the decisive day through faith in thee, O Maghavan.

Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche, o Indra, wagt sich an den, der dich besitzt? Im Vertrauen auf dich, du Gabenreicher, sucht am entscheidenden Tage der Preisk├дmpfer den Siegerpreis zu gewinnen.

Grassmann

Welch Sterblicher, o Indra, kann dem dir ergebnen Schaden thun? Wer dir vertraut, o m├дchtiger, am Tag der Schlacht, gewinnet Beute, beutereich.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAnimate (those men) for the destruction of their foes, who offer treasures which are dear to you, theabounder in wealth; may we, lord of bay steeds, along with (your) worshippers, pass over all difficulties by yourguidance.тАЭ

At the smashing of obstacles spur on the bounteous ones who give their own dear goods.
O you of the fallow bays, with your guidance may we, along with our patrons, overcome all difficulties.

And may we with our princes, Lord of Tawny Steeds! pass through all peril, led by thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYours, Indra, is the vast valuable wealth; you cherish the middling; you rule over all that which is themost precious; no one opposes you in (the recovering of the) cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na kis’ tva goс╣гu vriс╣Зvate = goс╣гu nimitteс╣гuke api tv─Бm na v─Бrayanti, none resist or oppose you on account of the cows

Jamison Brereton

Yours alone is the lowest good thing, Indra; you prosper the middling one.
You rule over each highest one entirely. No one obstructs you when cattle (are at stake).

Griffith

Thine, Indra, is the lowest wealth, thou cherishest the mid-most wealth,
Thou ever rulest all the highest: in the fray for cattle none resisteth thee.

Geldner

Dein, Indra, ist das unterste Gut, du mehrest das mittlere, du gebietest ├╝ber alles h├╢chste insgesamt. Nicht wehren sie dir im Kampf um die Rinder.

Grassmann

Das untre Gut ist, Indra, dein; das mittlere entfaltest du; Und ├╝ber alles obere gebietest du; dich hemmt man nicht, wenn’s Heerden gilt.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрд░реНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдзрдирджрд╛рдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╕рдиреН рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдГ рдЕрд╕рд┐ред рдп рдИрдВ рдп рдПрддреЗ рдЖрдЬрдпрдГ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рдкрд┐ рдзрдирджрд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЛрд╜рд╕рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдЕрдпрдВ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рдГ рдЬрдирдГ рддрд╡ ред рддреНрд╡рддреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдирд╛рдо рдЕрдиреНрдирдореБрджрдХрдВ рд╡рд╛ ред тАШрдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рдГ рдирд╛рдо’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрджрдХрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рдпрд╛рдЪрддреЗ ред рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are celebrated as the giver of wealth to all even where battles occur; all the people of theearth–desirous of protection, solicit you, the invoked of many.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dhanad─Б asi ┼Ыruto ya ─лm bhavantyaj─Бyaс╕е = yeete ─Бjayo yuddh─Бni bhavanti teс╣гu api dhanad─Бс╕е ┼Ыrutosi

Jamison Brereton

You are famed as the giver of spoils to everyone, whenever there are (battle-)drives.
Every earth-dweller here, when seeking help, desires a share in your name, o you who are invoked by many.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The relative clause of b, y├б ─лm bh├бvanti ─Бj├бyaс╕е, is very peculiar. There is no possible referent for the y├й in either the preceding or the following main clause, and in addition the ─лm lacks function. It seems like a mangled paraphrase of I.81.3 y├бd ud─л╠Бrata ─Бj├бyaс╕е тАЬwhen (battle-)drives arise/happen,тАЭ but what caused the mangling is unclear to me. The y├й can be by тАЬattractionтАЭ to the m. nom. pl. ─Бj├бyaс╕е from putative *y├бd, and this set of Indra hymns has several examples of functionless ─лm (VII.20.3, 21.1). But it still lacks motivation.

The VP n─Б╠Бma bhikс╣гate тАЬdesires a share in your nameтАЭ is striking and a little puzzling. The same phrase n─Б╠Бma тИЪbhaj is found in V.57.5, but there it means that the Maruts, the subjects of the verb, all share the same name. Here, by contrast, it must be a clever way of saying that everyone calls IndraтАЩs name, a novel paraphrase of the common epithet of Indra puruh┼лt├б- тАШcalled upon by manyтАЩ, found in this verse and vss. 20 and 26. (The English slang equivalent would be тАЬwants a piece of you.тАЭ) Geldner renders n─Б╠Бma bhikс╣гate as тАЬDeinen Namen fleht тАж anтАЭ (implores), robbing the expression of its vividness.

Griffith

Thou art renowned as giving wealth to every one in all the battles that are fought.
Craving protection, all these people of the earth, O Much-invoked, implore thy name.

Geldner

Du bist als der Geber jeglichen Schatzes ber├╝hmt, was es auch f├╝r K├дmpfe gibt. Deinen Namen fleht jeder schutzbed├╝rftige Erdenbewohner hier an, du Vielgerufener.

Grassmann

Ber├╝hmter Geber bist du jedes Kampfgewinns, wie viel der K├дmpfe auch entstehn; Und deinen Namen, vielgerufner, ruft allhier voll H├╝lfsbegier der Erdenmensch.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIf I were lord of as much (affluence) as you are, Indra, then might I support (your) worshippers,dispenser of wealth, and not squander it upon wickedness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If I were lord of as much as you are, Indra,
I would seek to make just my praiser (well) set up, you excavator of goods; I would not give him over to ill-estate.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root тИЪ─л┼Ы overwhelmingly takes the gen.; the construction here is identified by Grassmann (s.v. ─л┼Ы, col. 236: #8 mit dem Acc.) as mixed: the gen. y─Б╠Бvataс╕е is construed with the implied 2nd ps. тАЬas much as you are lord overтАЭ (y─Б╠Бvatas tv├бm [─л╠Б┼Ыiс╣гe]) in p─Бda a, which is picked up by the acc. et─Б╠Бvad in the contrary-to-fact тАЬif I were lord over so muchтАЭ (y├бd тАж et─Б╠Бvad ah├бm ─л╠Б┼Ыiya). I think it more likely that et─Б╠Бvad here is a quasi-adverbial summing up of the dependent clause; a more literal tr. would be тАЬif I were lord to such an extent asтАЭ or the like. The other passages assembled under GrassmannтАЩs #8 can be variously explained and do not provide strong evidence for an alternative case frame with тИЪ─л┼Ы. In III.18.3 y─Б╠Бvad is again adverbial; see the published translation тАЬinasmuch as I am master тАжтАЭ In VIII.68.7 ─л╠Б┼Ыe is properly construed with a gen. (kс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─лn─Б╠Бm) in its own p─Бda; the acc. cited by Grassmann, p┼лrvy─Б╠Бm ├бnuс╣гс╣нutim in the previous p─Бda, is probably an acc. of respect (see comm. ad loc.) For nearby VII.37.7 as well as III.51.4, the latter cited only as a possibility by Grassmann, see comm. ad locc.

Griffith

If I, O Indra, were the Lord of riches ample as thine own,
I should support the singer, God. who givest wealth! and not abandon him to woe.

Wenn, Indra, ich so viel des Guts bes├дsse, wie dir eigen ist, Dem S├дnger theilt ich reichlich zu, o G├╝terquell, nicht g├дb’ ich ihn dem Elend hin.

English translation:

тАЬMay I daily distribute wealth to the venerable wherever abiding; no other, Maghavan, than you is to besought by us; (no other is to us) a most excellent protector.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I would do my best just for the one who magnifies (the god) every day, to (bring him) wealth here wherever it is to be found,
for there exists no other, better friendship for us than you, nor even a father, bounteous one.

Griffith

Each day would I enrich the man who sang my praise, in whatsoever place he were.
No kinship is there better, Maghavan, than thine: a father even is no more.

Ich wollte spenden dem Verehrer Tag f├╝r Tag, des reichen Guts, wo er auch sei; Denn nichts ist werther uns als du, Verwandte nicht, o Held, und selbst der Vater nicht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe prompt offers (of praise), with solemn rites combined, acquires food; I bend down with adoration toyou, Indra, the invoker of many, as a carpenter bends the wooden circumference of the wheel.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is just the surpassing one who seeks to win the prize, as yokemate with Plenitude.
I bend Indra, invoked by many, here to you with a song, as a carpenter bends a felly made of good wood.

Griffith

With Plenty for his true ally the active man will gain the spoil.
Your Indra, Much-invoked, I bend with song, as bends a wright his wheel of solid wood.

Geldner

Nur der Meister will den Siegerpreis gewinnen mit der Wunscherf├╝llung im Bunde. Ich biege euch mit der Lobrede den vielgerufenen Indra her wie der Zimmermann eine Radfelge aus gutem Holze.

Grassmann

Wer eifrig ist, nur der erlangt mit Ueberfluss verbundnes Gut; Den vielgerufnen Indra bieg’ ich her durch Lied, wie Wagner sch├╢nen Rades Kranz.

English translation:

тАЬA man acquires not wealth by unbecoming praise; affluence devolves not upon one obstructing(sacrifice) in you, Maghavan, is the power whereby bounty (may be shown) to such as I am on the day of libation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Not by a bad(ly made) praise does a mortal find goods, nor will wealth reach the one who fails.
ItтАЩs an easy skill for you, bounteous oneтАФgiving to the likes of me on the decisive day.

A moral wins no riches by unworthy praise: wealth comes not to the niggard churl.
Light is the task to give, O Maghavan, to one like me on the decisive day.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe glorify you, hero, (Indra), the lord of all movable and stationary things, the beholder of the universe,with ladles filled (with Soma, like (the udders of) unmilked kine.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like udders: adugdha iva dhenavo = we praiseyou as unmilked kine praise their calves; the fullness of ladles, yath─Б dhenavaс╕е kс╣гirap┼лrс╣Зodhastvenavartante tad vat somap┼лrс╣Зa camastvena vartam─Бn─Б vayam bhс╣Ы┼Ыam abhiс╣г– umaс╕е, as the cows remain withthe state of the udders being full of milk, so we, abiding with the state of the ladle full of Soma, glorify you; Yajuс╣г27.35

Jamison Brereton

We keep bellowing to you, o champion, like unmilked cowsтАФ to you, Indra, who see (like) the sun, lord of this moving (world), lord of the still one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite GeldnerтАЩs easy тАЬdessen Auge die Sonne ist,тАЭ I cannot accept this for svardс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыam. First, dс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы- is never an тАШeyeтАЩ, but rather тАШseeingтАЩ or тАШhaving the appearance ofтАЩ, and furthermore, itтАЩs Varuс╣Зa who has the sun as his eye (that is, his spy). Here I think the point is rather that Indra, like the sun, sees everything in the world, here expressed by the merism тАЬthe moving and the still.тАЭ

Griffith

Like kine unmilked we call aloud, Hero, to thee, and sing thy praise,
Looker on heavenly light, Lord of this moving world, Lord, Indra, of what moveth not.

Geldner

Wir schreien nach dir, du Held, wie ungemolkene K├╝he, nach dem Herrn ├╝ber diese lebende Welt, nach dem Herrn ├╝ber die unbewegliche Natur, dessen Auge die Sonne ist, o Indra.

Grassmann

Wir schreien an, o Held, zumal wie ungemolkne K├╝he dich; Den himmelsgleichen, der du das, was geht, beherrschst, o Indra, und das Stehende.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдордШрд╡рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рднрд╡рдГ рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рддреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рджреГрд╢рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ рди рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рднрд╡реЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛рдирдиреНрдпреЛ рди рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡реЛ рд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛рдирдиреНрдпреЛ рди рдЬрд╛рддрдГ ред рди рдЪ рдЬрдирд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рдЪ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдкрд┐ рд▓реЛрдХреЗрд╖реБ рддреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рджреГрд╢рдГ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдиреНрдирд╛рд╕реНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рдирд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рее рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдордиреНрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдЧрд╛ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рдпрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣рд╡рд╛рдорд╣реЗ рд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛рдордГ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNo other such as you are, celestial or terrestrial, has been or will be born; desirous of horses, of food,of cattle affluent Indra, we invoke you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

There is no other heavenly one like you, nor earthly; neither born, nor to be born.
Seeking horses, seeking cows, vying for the prize, we call upon you, bounteous Indra.

Griffith

None other like to thee, of earth or of the heavens, hath been or ever will be born.
Desiring horses, Indra Maghavan! and kine, as men of might we call on thee.

Geldner

Kein anderer Himmlischer oder Irdischer ist dir gleich geboren oder wird geboren werden. Nach Rossen, nach Rindern verlangend rufen wir Preisk├дmpfer dich, du gabenreicher Indra.

Grassmann

Kein andrer ist im Himmel, auf der Erd’ wie du gewesen nicht, noch wird er sein; Nach Ross und Rind verlangend flehn wir, Indra, dich, o reicher, Opfer bringend an.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬElder Indra, bring that (wealth to me), being the junior, for, Maghavan, you have from the beginningbeen possessed of infinite treasure, and are to be adored at repeated sacrifices.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring this greater (good) here, Indra, to those who are lesser, for you, bounteous one, are from of old one with many goods, and the one to be called upon at every raid.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are two word plays in this verse. The simpler one is between the impv. bhara тАШbringтАЩ in p─Бda a and the ─Бmreс╕Нita bh├бre-bhare тАШat every raidтАЩ, where the noun bh├бra- has been specialized from тАШ(an occasion for) bearing awayтАЩ to тАШraidтАЩ.

The more complex one involves the creation and disappointment of expectations. The verse begins with abh─л╠Бс╣гat├бс╕е. The juxtaposition of these two forms 37 (the latter being the pres. part. to тИЪas тАШbeтАЩ in either gen.-abl. sg. or acc. pl.) and their close sandhi, with retroflex initial с╣г, invites the audience to fill in the semantics of the lexeme abh├н тИЪas тАШbe superiorтАЩ. But to our surprise, at the end of this hemistich we find the semantic opposite, k├бn─лyasaс╕е тАШthe lesser onesтАЩ, requiring us to revise our analysis of the opening, dissolving the presumed lexeme into the directional preverb/preposition abh├н and the independent pres. participle modifying k├бn─лyasaс╕е much later in the line. For extensive discussion see Oldenberg

I cannot follow Grassmann, Oldenberg in interpreting jy─Б╠Бyaс╕е as voc., but take it, with Geldner, as neut. sg. with t├бd. Among other things, AiG III.296 notes only two masc. vocatives in -─лyas in the RV, this one and ├│j─лyaс╕е in X.120.4, which is also better taken as a neut.

Griffith

Bring, Indra, the Victorious Ones; bring, elder thou, the younger host.
For, Maghavan, thou art rich in treasures from of old, and must be called in every fight.

Geldner

Zu denen, die die Kleineren sind, bringe, o Indra, das gr├╢├Яere Gut, denn du Gabenreicher bist von jeher der Schatzreiche und in jedem Kampfe anzurufen.

Grassmann

O Indra bring des Starken Schatz den besten auch des schw├дchern her; Denn reich bist du an allem Gut, o m├дchtiger, und rufenswerth in jeder Schlacht.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDrive away, Maghavan, our enemies; render riches easy of acquisition; be our preserver in war; be theaugmenter of (the prosperity) of (your) friends.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Thrust away the foes, bounteous one; make goods easy for us to find. Become a helper for us in (the contest for) great stakes; become a
strengthener of our comrades.

Griffith

Drive thou away our enemies, O Maghavan: make riches easy to be won.
Be thou our good Protector in the strife for spoil: Cherisher of our friends be thou.

Geldner

Grassmann

O stosse fort der Feinde Schar, o m├дchtiger, macht leicht erreichbar uns das Gut; Sei uns ein Helfer in dem grossen Kampfgew├╝hl, sei deiner Freunde F├╢rderer.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдХреНрд░рддреБрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЖ рднрд░ рдЖрд╣рд░ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдпрдерд╛ рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдзрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдзрдирдВ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ред рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░рд╛рд╣реВрдд рдпрд╛рдордирд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рдпрдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрд╢реАрдорд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBring to us, Indra, wisdom, as a father (gives knowledge) to his sons; bestow wealth upon us on thisoccasion, you the invoked of many, so that we, living at the solemnity may (long) enjoy the light (of existence).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, bring your resolve to bear for us, like a father for his sons. Do your best for us on this drive, you who are invoked by many. May we, (still) alive, reach the light.

Griffith

O Indra, give us wisdom as a sire gives wisdom to his sons.
Guide us, O Much-invoked, in this our way may we still live and look upon the light.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд) рдмрд╣реБрддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рднрдЧрд╡рдиреН ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рднрдЧрд╡рдиреН ! рдпрдерд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рддрдерд╛ рдирдГ рдХреНрд░рддреБрдорд╛рднрд░рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрд╛рдордирд┐ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдЮреНрдЫрд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдпрддреЛ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдЪрд╛рд╢реАрдорд╣рд┐ реереиремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдВрд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердиреАрдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдж рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рдХреНрд░рддреБрдореН) рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдЖ) (рднрд░) (рдкрд┐рддрд╛) (рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗрднреНрдпрдГ) (рдпрдерд╛) (рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛) рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡реНрдпрдЪреЛрд╜рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд (рдпрд╛рдордирд┐) рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рдордпреЗ (рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдГ) (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдВ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдЕрд╢реАрдорд╣рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо реереиремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ ! рдпрдерд╛ рдЬрдирдХреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреЛрд╖рдпрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдп рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╜рдкреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВ рджрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдпрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдп рдпрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╕рджреИрд╡рд╛рдирдиреНрджреЗрдо реереиремрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛рдГ) (рд╡реГрдЬрдирд╛рдГ) рд╡реГрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдпреИрд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рд╡рд╛ рддреЗ (рджреБрд░рд╛рдзреНрдпрдГ) рджреБрдГрдЦреЗрдирд╛рд╜рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдГ (рдорд╛) (рдЕрд╢рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ) рдЕрд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╡) (рдХреНрд░рдореБрдГ) рдЕрд╡рдХреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдпрдиреНрддреБ (рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛) [рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛] рд╕рд╣ (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рдкреНрд░рд╡рддрдГ) рдирд┐рдореНрдирд╛рдиреН (рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддреАрдГ) рдЕрдирд╛рджрд┐рднреВрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдЕрддрд┐) (рд╢реВрд░) рдирд┐рд░реНрднрдп (рддрд░рд╛рдорд╕рд┐) рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рдЩреНрдШреЗрдорд╣рд┐ реереиренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдЬрдирд╛рдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдГ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╢реНрдЪреЗрджреГрд╢реАрд░реНрдирд╛рд╡реЛ рд░рдЪрдпреЗрдпреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рддрд░реЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддрддреНрд░ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рдиреМрдЪрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдпрдерд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ реереиренрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдзрдирд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдорд┐рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрд░рд╛рдЬреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЬреАрд╡рдзрдирд╕рдВрдЪрдпреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдиреМрдпрд╛рдпрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рд░рд╛рдЬрдЬрди, рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рд╡ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рдЕрд╢рд╛ рдирд╛рд╡рд╛ рддрдпрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдд. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рддреВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдиреЗ рддрд░реВрди рдЬрд╛рд╡реЗ. рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рдд рдиреМрдХрд╛ рдЪрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдЪреЗ рдпрдерд╛рд░реНрде рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирен рее
